---
title: 'Food Affordability and Undernutrition'
date: '2024-09-14'
tags: ['UN', 'Food', 'Undernutrition']
draft: false
images: ['/static/images/food-affordabilty.png']
summary: Undernutrition and Food Affordability are issues that many countries today still deal with. It's estimated that around 381 million people around the world cannot afford an energy sufficient diet. With around 735 million people sufferring from malnutrition in 2023 it can be interesting to think about what it could possibly take to end issues such as undernutrition and obesity. Here we look at the median costs in regions for food affordability.
---

export const incomeExtent = d3.extent(data, d => d.Median)
export const populationExtent = d3.extent(data, d => parseInt(d.value.replace(/,/g, '')))
export const americas = data.filter((d) => d.region === "Americas");
export const europe = data.filter((d) => d.region === "Europe");
export const africa = data.filter((d) => d.region === "Africa");
export const asia = data.filter((d) => d.region === "Asia" || d.region === "Oceania");

export const parseDate = d3.timeParse("%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S.%LZ");
export const parsedDateTotal = total_growth.map((d) => {
    d.Year = parseDate(d.Year);
    return d;
});
export const parsedDateRelative = relative_growth.map((d) => {
    d.Year = parseDate(d.Year);
    return d;
});

export const extentRelative = d3.extent(relative_growth, (d) => d["Growth (%)"]);
export const extentTotal = d3.extent(total_growth, (d) => d["Change (%)"]);

export const extentPercentile = d3.extent(income_consumption_data, (d) => d['avg_welfare'])

export const AmericaSubset = income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Americas")
export const AmericaCountries= income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Americas").reduce((acc, cur) => {
  if (!acc[cur.country_code]) {
    acc[cur.country_code] = {
      country_code: cur.country_code,
      name: cur.name,
      year: cur.year,
      welfare_type: cur.welfare_type,
    };
  }
  acc[cur.country_code]["percentile" + cur.percentile] = (cur.avg_welfare.toFixed(2));
  return acc;
}, {});

export const AmericaMidpoints = Object.keys(AmericaCountries).map((key) => AmericaCountries[key]);
export const AmericaBounds = income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Americas").filter((d) => d.percentile == 90 || d.percentile == 10)
export const orderAmerica = d3.groupSort(AmericaSubset, (g) => d3.max(g, (d) => d["intermediate-region"]), (d) => d['country_code'])

export const EuropeSubset = income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Europe")
export const EuropeCountries= income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Europe").reduce((acc, cur) => {
  if (!acc[cur.country_code]) {
    acc[cur.country_code] = {
      country_code: cur.country_code,
      name: cur.name,
      year: cur.year,
      welfare_type: cur.welfare_type,
    };
  }
  acc[cur.country_code]["percentile" + cur.percentile] = (cur.avg_welfare.toFixed(2));
  return acc;
}, {});

export const EuropeMidpoints = Object.keys(EuropeCountries).map((key) => EuropeCountries[key]);
export const EuropeBounds = income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Europe").filter((d) => d.percentile == 90 || d.percentile == 10)
export const orderEurope = d3.groupSort(EuropeSubset, (g) => d3.max(g, (d) => d["sub-region"]), (d) => d['country_code'])

export const APSubset = income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Asia" || d["region"] == "Oceania")
export const APCountries= income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Asia" || d["region"] == "Oceania").reduce((acc, cur) => {
  if (!acc[cur.country_code]) {
    acc[cur.country_code] = {
      country_code: cur.country_code,
      name: cur.name,
      year: cur.year,
      welfare_type: cur.welfare_type,
    };
  }
  acc[cur.country_code]["percentile" + cur.percentile] = (cur.avg_welfare.toFixed(2));
  return acc;
}, {});

export const APMidpoints = Object.keys(APCountries).map((key) => APCountries[key]);
export const APBounds = income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Asia" || d["region"] == "Oceania").filter((d) => d.percentile == 90 || d.percentile == 10)
export const orderAP = d3.groupSort(APSubset, (g) => d3.max(g, (d) => d["sub-region"]), (d) => d['country_code'])

export const AfricaSubset = income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Africa")
export const AfricaCountries= income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Africa").reduce((acc, cur) => {
  if (!acc[cur.country_code]) {
    acc[cur.country_code] = {
      country_code: cur.country_code,
      name: cur.name,
      year: cur.year,
      welfare_type: cur.welfare_type,
    };
  }
  acc[cur.country_code]["percentile" + cur.percentile] = (cur.avg_welfare.toFixed(2));
  return acc;
}, {});

export const AfricaMidpoints = Object.keys(AfricaCountries).map((key) => AfricaCountries[key]);
export const AfricaBounds = income_consumption_data.filter((d) => d["region"] == "Africa").filter((d) => d.percentile == 90 || d.percentile == 10)
export const orderAfrica = d3.groupSort(AfricaSubset, (g) => d3.max(g, (d) => d["intermediate-region"]), (d) => d['country_code'])

Food Affordability and Undernutrition are issues that many parts of the world are still struggling to deal with. They are common issues that many people face. Undernutrition being a type of malnutrition typically occurs when an individual doesn't have enough to eat. It can happen for a variety of reasons a bad harvest due to drought, interregional conflicts that displace families, and poverty. Often, the causes are beyond the control of the people affected.

One of the most common reasons behind Undernutrition is due to the inability to afford having consistent meals. It's estimated 381 million people around the world cannot afford an energy sufficient diet. With around 735 million people sufferring from undernutrition in 2023. But is it an issue and how does it impact the lives of people who suffer from it?

For most people undernutrition weakens the immune system, it impacts focus and increases your risk for injuries. For individuals who end up hospitalized it lengthens the duration of stays. But for people who are pregnant, elderly or young children it can impact them the most. Around half of all child deaths under 5 are attributed to undernutrition.

Below we look at the costs and impacts of varying diets in respect to Food Affordability and Undernutrition throughout the world in relation to the impacts it can have on children.

<img alt="Food Affordability Chart" src="/static/images/food-affordabilty.png" className="w-full h-auto"/>

Link to Interactive: https://observablehq.com/d/834f962f53bbdb86

## Food Sufficiency and Outcomes

One of the biggest issues to do with undernutrition is how it impacts current and future generations. Almost 1.54 million child deaths were attributed to Low Birth Weights. While Infant Mortality Rates have gone down due to various things such as the use of medical techniques to assist with birthing issues still remain that often cannot be solved this way. The weight of the mother has an impact on the outcome of the child. While low cost solutions exist to help deal with these issues they aren't perfect. 

<img alt="Undernutrition Deaths Chart" src="/static/images/child-deaths-malnutrition-by-risk.png" className="w-full h-auto"/>

Let's briefly go over the types of diets that groups like the Food Administration Organization (FAO) look at and why they matter.

Energy Sufficient Diets deal with extreme undernutrition for issues such as wasting which typically occurs when an individual is below the normal range of weight for a given height. They provide the bare minimum amount of calories for an individual to be considered normal weight. While households may not be dying of starvation. When a household has a large amount of their daily income taken by just being able to eat it often impacts their perform their tasks in a society.

Nutrient Sufficient Diets deal with chronic undernutrition dealing with a deficiency of essential nutrients which impacts how the body grows. Nutrient Sufficient Diets deal with stunting which can have an impact on adult cognition later on in life. It impacts the ability for a child to learn with many children sufferring from stunting having lower cognitive abilities that non-stunted children. Changes to diet at any point in a childs life can significantly reduce the impacts of it on a childs performance.

Finally Healthy Diets. A Healthy Diet can vary depending on the culture they can be similarly priced to Nutrient Sufficient ones. Being able to afford a healthy diet isn't always correlated with better outcomes as obesity is an issue in many places. In the United States for example, households spend around the same amount on groceries as they do eating out.

Government subsidies and food programs could help households in regards to malnutrition both for obesity and undernutrition and many countries do exactly that. But its not always a priority for governments and for many it can be unaffordable.



## Regional Outcomes

Outcomes aren't always equal. While Europe and the Americas faired better than most. Across most regions countries still struggled with food insecurity. Let's look at how countries faired in their respective sub-regions.

<Beeswarm data={americas} extent={extentPercentile} radius={populationExtent} removeMiddle={true}/>
<ConsumptionBoxPlot data={AmericaSubset} midpoints={AmericaMidpoints} bounds={AmericaBounds} markers={costs.Americas} x={extentPercentile} y={orderAmerica} group={"intermediate-region"} width={1100} height={800}/>

For the most part in the Americas countries did well. Some Central and South American need more help than others. Outliers existed with Canada and the United States being much further ahead but struggling with other issues namely obesity. Meanwhile on the other end Haiti was worse off, it's likely that Cuba is in the same situation but there isn't any data to support this.

An interesting thing to note here is how small the difference between a nutrient sufficent diet and a healthy diet can be. But even then a healthy diet costing 33% of a household's income while a nutrient sufficient one only costing 10% of a households is quite a significant gap. Depending on income inequality as well the gap can be much larger than it can appear.

<Beeswarm data={europe} extent={extentPercentile} radius={populationExtent} removeMiddle={true}/>
<ConsumptionBoxPlot data={EuropeSubset} midpoints={EuropeMidpoints} bounds={EuropeBounds} markers={costs.Europe} x={extentPercentile} y={orderEurope} group={"sub-region"} width={1100} height={1100}/>

Europe was the only region to consist of the majority of countries that were able to afford healthy diets. Though, obesity rates in Europe have been on the rise this seems to be more due to an excess of calories. The nations that are trailing are still relatively new with many being former members of the Eastern Bloc.

<Beeswarm data={asia} extent={extentPercentile} radius={populationExtent}/>
<ConsumptionBoxPlot data={APSubset} midpoints={APMidpoints} bounds={APBounds} markers={costs.Asia} x={extentPercentile} y={orderAP} group={"sub-region"} width={1100} height={1425}/>

Asia and Oceania is a large subcategory. Encompassing regions such as the Middle East all the way to Polynesia. Median daily income tended to vary though East Asian countries tended to be the wealthiest. Russia also makes an appearance on this however, the accuracy of the results is questionable due to it likely referring to wages on the European side rather than in Siberia.

South Asia also makes a notable cluster and right next to it is another cluster of South East Asian countries that are also experiencing large population growths. These economies tend to be show growth but rural-urban inequalities in these nations like most Asian countries are high.

<Beeswarm data={africa} extent={extentPercentile} radius={populationExtent}/>
<ConsumptionBoxPlot data={AfricaSubset} midpoints={AfricaMidpoints} bounds={AfricaBounds} markers={costs.Africa} x={extentPercentile} y={orderAfrica} group={"intermediate-region"} width={1100} height={1425}/>

Africa is where the problems begin to arise. It's estimated by 2050 that 2 in 5 children will be born on the continent. From 2020 to 2050 it's expected for the population to increase by 50%. But in many parts of Africa real wages have been stagnate for decades.

<DivergingBoxPlot data={income_difference_data} annualDiff={annual_change_data}/>

<LineChart data={parsedDateRelative} extent={extentRelative} width={800} height={400} title={"Annual Average Real Wage Africa (2010-2020)"} x={"Year"} y={"Growth (%)"} id={"relative"}/>

Over the past decade real wage growth in Africa showed some growth coming into the decade but since then has seen a reversal of this trend. While food prices have been staying relatively consistent in increases with inflation for many African countries their economies are not growing enough to see any progress. With many countries becoming worse off since the previous decade.

<LineChart data={parsedDateTotal} extent={extentTotal} width={800} height={400} title={"Total Average Real Wage Growth Africa (2010-2020)"} x={"Year"} y={"Change (%)"} id={"total"}/>

It's a problem especially with climate change on the horizon. How the future of Africa is shaped could be a story about the diverging economies of nations and even possibly about the gap and differences between the Rural and Urban populations. But data on this is hard to come by and by the time any changes are made inequality could be embedded deep into these societies.

## Child Mortality

Malnutrition especially undernutrition is often a comorbidity that worsens infectious diseases such as the common flu to malaria. It does this by weakening the immune system reducing its ability to fight infections. It's especially a problem among elderly individuals and tends to be a common issue in increasing hospitalization of those impacted. 

But its impacts harm most people and children are no exception. Undernutrition reduces the bodies response to vaccines. Nearly half of all child deaths are linked to malnutrition. The problem can often start with the parents. With 1.54 million deaths attributed to malnutrition being caused due to low birth weights.
